WeatherPy¶

Note¶

  • Instructions have been included for each segment. You do not have to follow them exactly, but they are included to help you think through the steps.
In [1]:
# Dependencies and Setup
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import requests
import time
import openweathermapy as ow

# Import API key
from api_keys import api_key

# Incorporated citipy to determine city based on latitude and longitude
from citipy import citipy

# Output File (CSV)
output_data_file = "weather_output.csv"

# Range of latitudes and longitudes
lat_range = (-90, 90)
lng_range = (-180, 180)

Generate Cities List¶

In [2]:
# List for holding lat_lngs and cities
lat_lngs = []
cities = []

# Create a set of random lat and lng combinations
lats = np.random.uniform(low=-90.000, high=90.000, size=1500)
lngs = np.random.uniform(low=-180.000, high=180.000, size=1500)
lat_lngs = zip(lats, lngs)

# Identify nearest city for each lat, lng combination
for lat_lng in lat_lngs:
    city = citipy.nearest_city(lat_lng[0], lat_lng[1]).city_name
    
    # If the city is unique, then add it to a our cities list
    if city not in cities:
        cities.append(city)

# Print the city count to confirm sufficient count
len(cities)
Out[2]:
609

Perform API Calls¶

  • Perform a weather check on each city using a series of successive API calls.
  • Include a print log of each city as it's being processed (with the city number and city name).
In [3]:
# Define settings
settings = {"units": "imperial", "appid": api_key}

# Create list
data = []

# Loop through cities and retrieve data

print('Beginning Data Retrieval')
print('-------------------------------------------')

for city in cities:
    
    try: 
        print(f'Processing Record {cities.index(city)} | {city}')
        data.append(ow.get_current(city, **settings))
        
    except:
        print('City not found. Skipping...')

Convert Raw Data to DataFrame¶

  • Export the city data into a .csv.
  • Display the DataFrame
In [5]:
# Create empty dataframe with columns for city, latitude, longitude, temperature, humidity, cloudiness, and wind speed
weather_df = pd.DataFrame()
weather_df['City'] = ''
weather_df['Latitude'] = ''
weather_df['Longitude'] = ''
weather_df['Temperature'] = ''
weather_df['Humidity'] = ''
weather_df['Cloudiness'] = ''
weather_df['Wind Speed'] = ''

weather_df.head()
Out[5]:
City Latitude Longitude Temperature Humidity Cloudiness Wind Speed
In [6]:
# Add data to dataframe
for x in range(len(data)):
    weather_df.loc[x, 'City'] = data[x]("name")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Latitude'] = data[x]("coord.lat")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Longitude'] = data[x]("coord.lon")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Temperature'] = data[x]("main.temp_max")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Humidity'] = data[x]("main.humidity")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Cloudiness'] = data[x]("clouds.all")
    weather_df.loc[x, 'Wind Speed'] = data[x]("wind.speed")

weather_df.head()
Out[6]:
City Latitude Longitude Temperature Humidity Cloudiness Wind Speed
0 Falam 22.91 93.68 58.46 98 7 1.21
1 Thunder Bay 48.41 -89.26 39.99 48 40 6.93
2 Beringovskiy 63.05 179.32 29.66 92 100 3.85
3 Aklavik 68.22 -135.01 23 92 90 4.7
4 Hermanus -34.42 19.24 57 82 80 22.46
In [7]:
# Export data into a csv file
weather_df.to_csv(output_data_file)

Plotting the Data¶

  • Use proper labeling of the plots using plot titles (including date of analysis) and axes labels.
  • Save the plotted figures as .pngs.

Latitude vs. Temperature Plot¶

In [8]:
plt.scatter(weather_df['Latitude'], weather_df['Temperature'])

plt.xlabel('Latitude')
plt.ylabel('Maximum Temperature (F)')
plt.title('City Latitude vs. Maximum Temperature (2019/11/03)')
plt.ylim(min(weather_df['Temperature'])-5,max(weather_df['Temperature'])+5)

# Save the Figure
plt.savefig('City Latitude vs. Maximum Temperature.png')

# Show the Figure
plt.show()

Latitude vs. Humidity Plot¶

In [9]:
plt.scatter(weather_df['Latitude'], weather_df['Humidity'])

plt.xlabel('Latitude')
plt.ylabel('Humidity (%)')
plt.title('City Latitude vs. Humidity (2019/11/03)')
plt.ylim(0-5,100+5)

# Save the Figure
plt.savefig('City Latitude vs. Humidity.png')

# Show the Figure
plt.show()

Latitude vs. Cloudiness Plot¶

In [10]:
plt.scatter(weather_df['Latitude'], weather_df['Cloudiness'])

plt.xlabel('Latitude')
plt.ylabel('Cloudiness (%)')
plt.title('City Latitude vs. Cloudiness (2019/11/03)')
plt.ylim(0-5,100+5)

# Save the Figure
plt.savefig('City Latitude vs. Cloudiness.png')

# Show the Figure
plt.show()

Latitude vs. Wind Speed Plot¶

In [11]:
plt.scatter(weather_df['Latitude'], weather_df['Wind Speed'])

plt.xlabel('Latitude')
plt.ylabel('Wind Speed (mph)')
plt.title('City Latitude vs. Wind Speed (2019/11/03)')
plt.ylim(0-2,max(weather_df['Wind Speed'])+2)

# Save the Figure
plt.savefig('City Latitude vs. Wind Speed.png')

# Show the Figure
plt.show()

Observations¶

Based on the weather data of random cities obtained through the Open Weather API, I would like to highlight the following observations. Firstly, the maximum temperature ranges from around -20F to 100F. The maximum temperature is highest in cities near the equator (latitude 0). Secondly, humidity and cloudiness range from 0% to 100%. Many cities have either 0% or 100% cloudiness. There is no clear trend in humidity or cloudiness with varying distance from the equator. Lastly, wind speed ranges from 0mph to around 40mph. The wind speed of most cities is between 0mph and 10mph. The cities with the highest wind speeds tend to be farther away from the equator.
